<div id="review_491387211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491387211" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8710948-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459396170p2/8710948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491387211?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/8710948-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491387211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16258278430318653955">This book.. I have so many mixed feelings about this book. From the start I was so intrigued because the main character herself was unsure of her own innocence, but that made sense and was completely explained in just a few chapters. The further I read the more and more convoluted things got and more twisted everyone became. Everyone looked like a suspect, but if you read enough murder mystery stories it is admittedly pretty easy to step outside the box and guess what happened. <br/><br/>The parents.. I d</span>
  <span id="freeText16258278430318653955" style="display:none">This book.. I have so many mixed feelings about this book. From the start I was so intrigued because the main character herself was unsure of her own innocence, but that made sense and was completely explained in just a few chapters. The further I read the more and more convoluted things got and more twisted everyone became. Everyone looked like a suspect, but if you read enough murder mystery stories it is admittedly pretty easy to step outside the box and guess what happened. <br /><br />The parents.. I didn't know whether they were monsters or just.. parents. They obviously loved their children but they were so demanding of them that it bordered negligent and the entire idea of enforcing your children to be sociopaths seemed, foreign isn't the right word, but... off. I understand blocking out emotions, but considering emotional outbursts shameful are... Hmm. These two were never seen alive in the entire book and yet I still have no idea how to feel about them. <br /><br />As for the kids they were all lovable and handled a bad situation in a way that would have made their parents proud. Each one of them I fell in love with a little bit because they were real... They were just kids who had been caught in something bigger than they would have ever known but they were also brilliant and tough and completely determined to do whatever they had to do. <br /><br />All in all, I love this book from it's plot to it's characters. The ending of it made me cry, honestly and truly it did. I can very honestly say I'll be disappointed if there isn't a sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16258278430318653955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_569650114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569650114" />
    <a title="Adrienne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8482982-adrienne"><img alt="Adrienne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560275112p2/8482982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569650114?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrienne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrienne" href="/user/show/8482982-adrienne">Adrienne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316206983" href="/book/show/13528399-confessions-of-a-murder-suspect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8482982-adrienne?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8482982-adrienne?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8482982-adrienne?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer569650114&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569650114" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7779824291773723471">This book was told in a very persuasive narrative that had me second-guessing about what really happened to Malcolm and Maud Angel, two extremely successful (and cunning) entrepreneurs who were found dead in bed. They had four highly intelligent and exceptionally gifted children -- Matthew, Tandoori, Harry ♥ and Hugo -- who were labeled as the prime suspects for murder especially after they showed no remorse or sadness for their parents' death. But the Angel kids weren't exactly what you'd call </span>
  <span id="freeText7779824291773723471" style="display:none">This book was told in a very persuasive narrative that had me second-guessing about what really happened to Malcolm and Maud Angel, two extremely successful (and cunning) entrepreneurs who were found dead in bed. They had four highly intelligent and exceptionally gifted children -- Matthew, Tandoori, Harry ♥ and Hugo -- who were labeled as the prime suspects for murder especially after they showed no remorse or sadness for their parents' death. But the Angel kids weren't exactly what you'd call "normal". They turned out the way they did because of the constant pressure that their parents had put them under and because of the "multivitamins" that they had drunken everyday which supposedly enhanced their memory, speed and agility. But these pills weren't exactly harmless; they were designed to turn the Angel kids into bland, emotionless people who didn't have a conscience. They were being experimented on using the drugs that their own father and uncle had manufactured.<br /><br />Matthew, the eldest brother, was prone to angry outbursts that more or less resulted in violence which was why he was considered as the main suspect by the police. Tandy, his younger sister and the protagonist in this book, was viewed as a robot practically incapable of feeling human emotions which was why she was also considered as the murderer (because, you know, sociopaths don't have feelings and all). Her twin, Harry (oh how I love that name! ♥) was her exact opposite -- you could always tell when he was going to have a meltdown. He seemed like the guilty one in the book (because he was the only one crying among the Angel kids) so the police didn't rule him out of being a possible suspect. Hugo, the youngest, had quite a bit of a temper and liked smashing, breaking, punching, kicking or physically assaulting <i>anything</i> from an inanimate object to a living, breathing organism. There was no doubt he was capable of injuring somebody, even if he was just a ten-year-old kid. But I had no suspicions on him; none at all.<br /><br />I honestly thought <i>someone</i> had murdered Malcolm and Maud, especially since the narrator kept turning me around in circles and pointing her finger at suspect after suspect after suspect. I thought some big dramatic confrontation would ensue and that someone would get shot or something. But no, the ending turned out to be a big anticlimactic finale. It wasn't murder that had taken place, it was <i>suicide.</i> Malcolm and Maud's death was a twisted semblance of Romeo and Juliet's; both of them taking their lives because one couldn't bear living without the other. Awfully surprising really. I had assumed it was cold-blooded murder done out of spite or jealousy. There were still some unanswered questions left at the end though that had me searching for the sequel to this one. Hopefully, I'll be able to get my hands on the next book and enjoy another suspense-filled mystery novel by James Patterson.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7779824291773723471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_807909783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/807909783" />
    <a title=" M (Inactive because school) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14044727-m-inactive-because-school"><img alt=" M (Inactive because school) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431164075p2/14044727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/807909783?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" M (Inactive because school) " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" M (Inactive because school) " href="/user/show/14044727-m-inactive-because-school"> M (Inactive because school) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14044727-m-inactive-because-school?shelf=regrets">regrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer807909783&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer807909783" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10982343589204157149"><b>2 stars.<br/><i>She can’t trust anyone.<br/>Maybe not even herself.</i></b><br/><br/>I could define the whole book in one word: <b>BLAND</b>. It’s not worth the time, and the money. I’m really disappointed because I thought this one would be a great read to start another year. But I was wrong. I was painfully wrong. <br/><br/>I didn’t like the main character Tandy Angel. I don’t know, yeah she’s smart, pretty and rich. I just didn’t like her. She just ticked me off. I feel bad because I’m saying this right now but I don’t wanna lie and preten</span>
  <span id="freeText10982343589204157149" style="display:none"><b>2 stars.<br /><i>She can’t trust anyone.<br />Maybe not even herself.</i></b><br /><br />I could define the whole book in one word: <b>BLAND</b>. It’s not worth the time, and the money. I’m really disappointed because I thought this one would be a great read to start another year. But I was wrong. I was painfully wrong. <br /><br />I didn’t like the main character Tandy Angel. I don’t know, yeah she’s smart, pretty and rich. I just didn’t like her. She just ticked me off. I feel bad because I’m saying this right now but I don’t wanna lie and pretend that I liked this book. I expected her to be the killer. But no, she didn’t kill her parents because they had suicide. They had suicide because they were weak. And left their children the world to carry. On. Their. Own. Tandy could have also been more likable if her role in the story was more than to avenge the death of her parents by trespassing into people’s house. But must say, she really was smart. Not-so-bad smart.<br /><br />Plus, the story didn’t have a catch. I didn’t even think it had a climax. Seriously, mysteries make my heart pound but this one just, meh. It was very plain and uncompelling. There was not much highs and lows because the whole story was a plain horizontal line: <b>no movement</b>. <br /><br />The other characters were very incompetent. Maybe Hugo was the only character who had spice. I kind of liked him, but just kind of. And then their parents—their dead parents—were pervs. Seriously? Maud, their mom, had a relationship with her female assistant? And their Dad slept with his son’s girlfriend? Wow. Bland and un-timingly freakin’ Bizarroville. Crazy town in the sense that you would have the urge to throw this book out your window.<br /><br />Okay. I was harsh. But I’m trying my best not to be. Anyway, maybe I should praise Patterson for creating Hugo. I really got interested in Hugo. The rest of the book, well, wasn’t so decisive. To be honest, I feel so sorry for myself and for Patterson. He could have made Tandy the killer. That would have been better. And at least there’s a good part in the end: the epilogue. Freeing-the-sharks drama. Beautiful. <br /><br />But anyway, I should really be careful in choosing books to read. Because not all books are worth the time. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10982343589204157149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_468180691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468180691" />
    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7373562-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326071350p2/7373562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468180691?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/7373562-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468180691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13813978462400467627">I didn't know how to feel about this book when I finished it. I didn't know whether I liked it or hated it. I also think I am being a little generous with the star-rating. So maybe I'm leaning more towards didn't like. But there's a reason for my mixed opinion. This book was confused. I mean it was written that way. <br/><br/>Tandy was the daughter of the Angels, an elite family well known for the amazingly talanted offspring they produced. Every single one of there children have a talent. Tandy the unemo</span>
  <span id="freeText13813978462400467627" style="display:none">I didn't know how to feel about this book when I finished it. I didn't know whether I liked it or hated it. I also think I am being a little generous with the star-rating. So maybe I'm leaning more towards didn't like. But there's a reason for my mixed opinion. This book was confused. I mean it was written that way. <br /><br />Tandy was the daughter of the Angels, an elite family well known for the amazingly talanted offspring they produced. Every single one of there children have a talent. Tandy the unemotional smart one, Matty the strong and fast football player, Harry the emotional artist, and Hugo the unbelieveably strong 10 year old. Their parents Maud and Malcom were poisened in their bedroom in the middle of the night. So natrually, everyone in the house at the time of death were suspects. Hence the title. <br /><br />I did have problems with the story itself but I want to talk about my main issue to keep this short, and most of my issues were with the writing. It's different. Different can be good or bad really and this book was a little of both for me. We read from Tandys point of view though actually she is writing her story to us, the readers. I really liked this. It made me feel more involved in the story. But she was confused about, well everything. which in turn left me confused and irritated throughout most of the book.<br /><br />Tandy, our "writer " would start to talk about something, like some memory she had, and then stop and just move on saying she will talk about it later, completely leaving you hanging. Then you get thrown back into the story and just when you got comfortable with that subject she'd change it up again. So I never really got into the rhythm of the book, and was constantly dissappointed. Not to mention the chapters were only like three or four pages long so it really was like she couldn't finish a complete thought and the book was kinda choppy. There were also a LOT of questions left unanswered. So either they are going to leave it at that or there's another one coming, which I can honestly say I am not all that excited for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13813978462400467627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_864063633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864063633" />
    <a title="Kate ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27335378-kate"><img alt="Kate ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388879906p2/27335378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/864063633?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate ★" href="/user/show/27335378-kate">Kate ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27335378-kate?shelf=the-a-z-challenge-2014">the-a-z-challenge-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864063633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3497269368836346731">I feel so bad having to rate this as two stars because I am a James Patterson fan. However, I could not really lie to myself so I'm just going to have to put in my honest review.<br/><br/>I started out liking the book. Parents found murdered inside their own room with 3 of their children inside the house. How was it possible that no one heard them scream? How was it possible that they were killed right under the residents' noses? Who had the motive for doing such a horrendous act?<br/><br/>As the story went deeper,</span>
  <span id="freeText3497269368836346731" style="display:none">I feel so bad having to rate this as two stars because I am a James Patterson fan. However, I could not really lie to myself so I'm just going to have to put in my honest review.<br /><br />I started out liking the book. Parents found murdered inside their own room with 3 of their children inside the house. How was it possible that no one heard them scream? How was it possible that they were killed right under the residents' noses? Who had the motive for doing such a horrendous act?<br /><br />As the story went deeper, this big closet of secrets was opened and the skeletons came tumbling out. Tandoori or Tandi, one of the Angel children, is the narrator in the story. Her goal was to find out the real killer, even if it meant convicting one of her siblings. Each of them were put into focus. Matthew, the NFL star who disagreed with his parents; Harry, the child prodigy who never felt loved; Hugo, the war-freak boy who received the biggest chop and admitted he wanted his parents dead; and Tandoori, who saw herself as a bird in a cage. Everything about the Angel family was bizarre! In fact, I had a hard time buying that such a twisted family would exist.<br /><br />The focus was then turned to the mysterious drugs that the kids had been taking. The story went downhill at this point. I was bored reading about those stupid meds and the effect they had on the children. I've had enough of Tandoori playing detective because I find her self-important, as her uncle Peter called her.<br /><br />The ending was rather disappointing. I had my suspicions on what happened and turned out I was right. What their parents did wasn't an act of sacrifice as it an act of selfishness. Did they consider what would happen to their children? Did they even think about how they would be branded as murderers? Had the kids not found that video, they were bound to be doomed. What kind of parents would do that?<br /><br />A lot of questions remained unanswered. I'm still going to read the next book because I still love James Patterson. This just didn't go well for me. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="3497269368836346731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_430866717" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430866717" />
    <a title="Once" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3515991-once"><img alt="Once" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294165894p2/3515991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430866717?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Once" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Once" href="/user/show/3515991-once">Once</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430866717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14164831972310560417">James Patterson, one of the most well known authors, some how continues to produce amazing series. With the Maximum Ride, Daniel X, and Witch and Wizard series reaching millions of readers, it seems that maybe Mr. Patterson would take a break. Thankfully this is not the case with the renowned author's new novel Confessions of A Murder Suspect. Written with his extremely visual writing style, Patterson drifts away from his genre of fantasy and science fiction and goes to a more realistic mystery </span>
  <span id="freeText14164831972310560417" style="display:none">James Patterson, one of the most well known authors, some how continues to produce amazing series. With the Maximum Ride, Daniel X, and Witch and Wizard series reaching millions of readers, it seems that maybe Mr. Patterson would take a break. Thankfully this is not the case with the renowned author's new novel Confessions of A Murder Suspect. Written with his extremely visual writing style, Patterson drifts away from his genre of fantasy and science fiction and goes to a more realistic mystery with a secondary author by the name of Maxine Paetro. The novel uses many dramatic twists and really portrays the emotional aspect of the book. The quest for perfection is highlighted to the extreme in this book! <br /><br />In the novel we follow teenager Tandy Angel who awakens one night to find that her parents have been murdered. The murder seems almost impossible to commit from an outsider making Tandy and her brothers instant suspects. Now Tandy's parents were no ordinary parents. They just so happened to be extremely rich parents. Tandy and her siblings have led a highly cultured life, in where their parents control everything to achieve perfection. This control however, sadly turns each sibling into a type of sociopath which Tandy realizes makes them prime suspects. While dealing with the conflicting feelings of loss for her parents, Tandy does vow to find the killer and bring them to justice. <br /><br />An emotional roller coaster, this novel thrives off of dramatic twists and surprises. As always Patterson does a wonderful job of composing his characters. My only wish for this new book of Patterson, is that would be longer, providing more back story. I feel it would have greatly enhanced the over story. Nevertheless, this is a great book, and will surely become a best-seller!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14164831972310560417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_873460241" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/873460241" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/873460241?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316207003" href="/book/show/17182352-confessions-of-a-murder-suspect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873460241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12918936618779716895">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>16-year-old Tandy and her siblings are the only people in the house the night their parents are discovered dead.<br/>Who killed Tandy’s parents? And why did they name her Tandoori?<br/><br/><br/>The characters in this were all nuts, and the storyline was pretty darn boring considering that people were dead!<br/><br/>I didn’t like Tandoori, and not just because I wasn’t a fan of her name. She just said the strangest things, she thought the strangest things, her upbringing was bizarre, and s</span>
  <span id="freeText12918936618779716895" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />16-year-old Tandy and her siblings are the only people in the house the night their parents are discovered dead.<br />Who killed Tandy’s parents? And why did they name her Tandoori?<br /><br /><br />The characters in this were all nuts, and the storyline was pretty darn boring considering that people were dead!<br /><br />I didn’t like Tandoori, and not just because I wasn’t a fan of her name. She just said the strangest things, she thought the strangest things, her upbringing was bizarre, and she didn’t even show how upset she was that her parents were dead. It was no wonder that she was a suspect!<br /><br />The storyline in this was okay I suppose, but the execution let it down. Every character in this book was psychologically damaged in some way, and even the stories about their childhood were just bizarre, and not in a good way. I got really fed up of this crazy nonsense pretty early on, and could not finish this fast enough. If these were real people I’d be calling a psychiatrist to section them all, and probably calling social services to have the children taken away, as Tandoori’s parents were pretty shocking parents. Telling your child that they’re ‘damaged’ because they show emotion is absolutely terrible, and disowning your three-year-old for being afraid on a rollercoaster is utterly nutty.<br />The ending was okay, and I was glad to find out what actually happened. I was also glad that it was over though.<br />Overall; crazy characters and a messed up storyline,<br />4.5 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12918936618779716895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wR8mBSriNpI3WNeFFNcd8dQEUH6/ZDU95a/ecJJhZdZSSy3mGdcNoE+T1uE1Hw0cV3XLsK91S8aTOmmPuZ2NBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sMaWHdQMRJn1wweGLMBf3shreiTKBrSMRWVSuN4fjZQjkp3+5zl/q40IBuINCE8zSxrh6toXyncz8OVH9eNlRA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4122890545797964575"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText4122890545797964575" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
  <a data-text-id="4122890545797964575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
